Collection\n\n1. **Scene Management**  \n   - Secure the device in a Faraday bag to stop remote access.  \n   - Document battery status, screen lock, and any visible damage.  \n   - Photograph the or Oxygen Forensic Detective in *Full Extraction* mode.  \n   - Verify SHA\u2011256 and MD5 checksums of the raw image.  \n\n4. **Chain of Custody**  \n   - Complete a chain of custody form for every hand\u2011off.  \n   - Store the original device and image in a secure evidence locker.\n\n#### Phase 2 \u2013 Examination\n\n1. **Mounting & Hash Verification**  \n   - Mount the raw image in Autopsy.  \n   - Verify that the image\u2019s file system hash matches the acquisition hash.  \n\n2. **File System Walkthrough**  \n   - Identify key directories: `/data`, `/data/system`, `/sdcard` that reference GPS or network connectivity.\n\n#### Phase 3 \u2013 Analysis\n\n##### 3.1 Location Retrieval\n\n| Source | Artefact | Extraction Method |\n|--------|-----------|-------------------|\n| Google Location History | `GoogleLocationHistory.db` | SQLite3 query: `SELECT latitudeE7, longitudeE7, time, accuracy FROM location_history ORDER BY time;` |\n| Samsung Cloud | `SamsungHealth.db` | DB Browser read `location` table |\n| Wi\u2011Fi Scan Log | `/data/misc/wifi/` | Extract `wpa_supplicant.conf` or `wifi0`/`wifi1` DBs |\n| Cell Tower | `/data/misc/telephony/` | Extract `telephony.db` (msisdn, cellId, lac) |\n| 3rd\u2011party Navigations | Waze, HERE | Extract `waze.db`, `here.db` |\n| System Logs | `/system/etc/` | grep `GPS` or `LocationProvider` |\n\n6. **Timestamp Normalisation**  \n   - Convert all timestamps to UTC.  \n   - Adjust for device clock drift by comparing with known GPS epoch times.  \n\n7. **GIS Mapping**  \n   - Import the cleaned CSV into QGIS.  \n   - Plot points and create a line connecting them.  \n   - Overlay points on a map of the suspect\u2019s residence and the crime scene.  \n\n8. **Cross\u2011Verification**  \n   - Match GPS points with Wi\u2011Fi SSID logs (e.g., \u201cHomeWifi\u201d).  \n   - Verify cell tower IDs with the carrier\u2019s public cell tower database to approximate location.  \n   - If available, request the carrier for CDRs covering 15\u202fJan\u202f2024 to confirm network attachment.\n\n9. **Confidence Assessment**  \n   - Assign confidence levels:  \n     - 1\u202f=\u202fGPS (high)  \n     - 2\u202f=\u202fWi\u2011Fi (moderate)  \n     - 3\u202f=\u202fCell (low)  \n   - Document reasons for each classification.\n\n10. **Narrative Construction**  \n    - Build a day\u2011by\u2011day timeline.  \n    - Highlight the time window of the murder (as known from other evidence).  \n    - Show whether the suspect was at or near the crime scene during that window.\n\n##### 3.2 Supporting Artefacts\n\n- **App Usage Logs** \u2013 e.g., Waze \u201cTrip\u201d logs that show a route taken.  \n- **Bluetooth LE Beacon Logs** \u2013 possible proximity to the victim\u2019s phone.  \n- **SMS/Call Logs** \u2013 if a call at the murder time was placed from a specific location.  \n- **Social Media Check\u2011Ins** \u2013 Facebook/Instagram, if any.\n\n#### Phase 4 \u2013 Reporting\n\n1. **Executive Summary** \u2013 concise answer to the question (yes/no, with timeline).  \n2. **Methodology Section** \u2013 detail each NIST phase, tools used, and justification.  \n3. **Evidence Section** \u2013 list of artefacts, hash values, and extraction dates.  \n4. **Analysis Section** \u2013 tables of GPS/Wi\u2011Fi/cell points, GIS map screenshots, confidence ratings.  \n5. **Conclusion** \u2013 definitive answer: \u201cThe suspect was located at X address between 02:30\u201103:45\u202fUTC on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024, which overlaps with the estimated time of the murder.\u201d  \n6. **Appendices** \u2013 screenshots, raw data excerpts, chain of custody.  \n7. **Signature & Date** \u2013 forensic examiner\u2019s credentials and digital signature.  \n\n---\n\n## Justification of the Methodology\n\n| NIST Phase | Why This Approach? | Tool Benefit |\n|------------|--------------------|--------------|\n| **Collection** | Preserve original state and create a Function | Tool | Reason for Selection |\n|-----------|------|----------------------|\n| Device imaging | Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer | Industry standard, handles modern Android encryption. |\n| Put the phone in **EMF shielded** environment. <br>- Use a **write blocker** (if the phone can be connected via USB). <br>- Acquire a **full logical image** (and if possible a **physical image**) of the internal storage. <br>- Verify hash (SHA\u2011256/MD5). | \u2022 **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** (supports full logical/physical for Android). <br>\u2022 **Magnet AXIOM** (Android). <br>\u2022 **Open\u2011Source**: **FTK Imager** + **ADB** for logical extraction. |\n| **2.1.3**\u202fCollect external artefacts | Cloud data, carrier logs, and other remote services may hold location data. | - Identify and request Google/OneDrive/WhatsApp backups, Cloud\u2011based map logs, Samsung Cloud. <br>- Obtain carrier call/SMS/location logs via lawful intercept or court order. <br>- Capture network traffic if the phone was connected to Wi\u2011Fi at the time. | \u2022 **Carrier portal** (e.g., AT&T, Verizon). <br>\u2022 **Google Takeout**. <br>\u2022 **Wi\u2011Fi\u2011Net** for capturing Wi\u2011Fi handshakes. |\n| **2.1.4**\u202fPreserve physical device | The phone may contain volatile data (RAM, battery\u2011driven GPS). | - Use **Li\u2011ion\u2011battery\u2011preservation** procedures. <br>- Record battery level, temperature. <br>- If permitted, capture a **RAM dump** with a tool that can interface with Android (e.g., **LiDAR** or **ADB\u2011root**). | \u2022 **Android Debug Bridge (ADB)** (for memory dump in rooted devices). <br>\u2022 **ADB\u2011M** for memory capture. |\n\n> **Why this order?**  \n> The raw data must be captured first; any later manipulation could contaminate the evidence.  \n> External artefacts are gathered concurrently because they may be lost if the phone is powered off later.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Phase 2 \u2013 **Examination** (Data\u2011Recovery & Artefact Extraction)\n\n| Step | Rationale | Key Activities | Recommended Tools |\n|------|-----------|----------------|-------------------|\n| **3.2.1**\u202fVerify image integrity | Ensure nothing changed during acquisition. | - Detailed Methodology\n\n### 2.1 Phase\u202f1 \u2013 Collection\n\n1. **Scene & Device Handling**\n   - Photograph the device in its seized state (case, accessories, markings).\n   - Record serial number, IMEI, and any visible damage.\n   - Signatures at each transfer point.\n\n3. **Write\u2011Protected Imaging**\n   - Use a **write\u2011blocker** (e.g., Cellebrite UFED\u2011Pro) to connect the phone to a forensic workstation.\n   - Create a **bit\u2011by\u2011bit (dd) image** of the internal storage (`/data`, `/system`, `/cache`) and the **eMMC** if accessible.\n   - Extract **active processes**, **network connections**, **Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs** currently connected.\n   - If the device is off, note that volatile data will be unavailable.\n\n5. **Metadata Preservation**\n   - **SMS/Call Logs**: `mmssms.db`.\n   - **Calendar & Notes**: `calendar.db`, `notes.db`.\n   - **Browser History**: `chrome` or `firefox` history for location\u2011related searches.\n\n   Use **Cellebrite** or **XDA\u2011Android** to pull encrypted app databases; if encryption is present, attempt to recover keys via **Android KeyStore** or **rooted\u2011device** extraction (if the device is rooted).\n\n3. **Preservation**\n   - Wi\u2011Fi & BLE Mapping** | Match SSIDs/BLE MACs to known venues via **Wi\u2011Fi\u2011DB** or **Indoor Positioning** services. | Adds context (e.g., coffee shop, mall). | `wifi\u0654db`, `bluetooth\u2011scanner` |\n| **D. Gap Analysis** | Identify periods with no location data. | Determine if the suspect was offline, battery\u2011off, or using a \u201ckill\u2011switch\u201d. | Custom Python script |\n| **G. Justification of the Methodology\n\n| NIST Phase | Why It Is Needed in This Case |\n|------------|------------------------------|\n| **Collection** | The suspect\u2019s phone may contain volatile data (e.g., active Wi\u2011Fi connections) that would be lost if the device is powered off. A forensic image preserves all data for later analysis. |\n| **Examination** | The phone\u2019s file system is complex; automated tools ensure no artifact is missed. Extracting all relevant logs is essential to reconstruct the timeline. |\n| **Analysis** | Multiple independent location sources (GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi) are required to overcome gaps and increase accuracy. Correlating timestamps resolves inconsistencies. |\n| **Reporting** | The final product must be clear, reproducible, and defensible. Visual aids and confidence metrics help the court understand the evidence. |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Practical Tips & Pitfalls\n\n1. **Battery\u2011Off Device**  \n   - If the phone is off, you will lose GPS, Wi\u2011Fi, and cell logs for the period it was off.  \n   - Mitigation: Use **cell\u2011tower** and **app** logs that may still be present in the file system.\n\n2. **Encrypted Data**  \n   - Many Android apps encrypt their databases.  \n   - Mitigation: Use **Cellebrite**\u2019s decryption engine or attempt to recover the **Android Keystore** if the device is rooted.\n\n3. **Time\u2011Zone & Clock Drift**  \n   - Android devices may have incorrect clocks.  \n   - Mitigation: Cross\u2011check with **NTP** logs or with timestamps from other devices (e.g., suspect\u2019s smartwatch).\n\n4. **Location Accuracy**  \n   - GPS accuracy can vary (urban canyons, indoors).  \n   - Mitigation: Include **accuracy** field in the report and use **confidence intervals**.\n\n5. **Legal Compliance**  \n   - Ensure all steps comply with local laws (e.g., warrant, privacy).  \n   - Keep a **log of all actions** (tool commands, timestamps).\n\n---\n\n## 6. Expected Outcome\n\nBy following the above methodology, investigators should be able to produce a **timeline of the suspect\u2019s movements on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024** with at least **\u00b1\u202f50\u202fm confidence** for GPS points and **\u00b1\u202f500\u202fm confidence** for cell\u2011tower points. Detailed Methodology\n\n### 2.1 Phase\u202f1 \u2013 Collection\n\n1. **Scene & Device Handling**\n   - Photograph the device in its seized state (case, accessories, markings).\n   - Record serial number, IMEI, and any visible damage.\n   - Note battery status (charged, depleted) and whether the device is locked.\n\n2. **Chain of Custody**\n   - Fill out a **Chain\u2011of\u2011Custody (CoC)** form (date, time, personnel, actions).\n   - Signatures at each transfer point.\n\n3. **Write\u2011Protected Imaging**\n   - Use a **write\u2011blocker** (e.g., Cellebrite UFED\u2011Pro) to connect the phone to a forensic workstation.\n   - Create a **bit\u2011by\u2011bit (dd) image** of the internal storage (`/data`, `/system`, `/cache`) and the **eMMC** if accessible.\n   - Compute **MD5/SHA\u2011256** checksums of the raw image and store them in a secure log.\n\n4. **Volatile Data Capture**\n   - If the device is powered on, capture **RAM** using a tool that supports Android (e.g., **Cellebrite UFED** or **XDA\u2011Android**).\n   - Extract **active processes**, **network connections**, **Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs** currently connected.\n   - If the device is off, note that volatile data will be unavailable.\n\n5. **Metadata Preservation**\n   - Record the **device\u2019s firmware version**, **Android version**, **carrier**, and **SIM card** details.\n   - Capture **system logs** (`logcat`) if possible.\n\n### 2.2 Phase\u202f2 \u2013 Examination\n\n1. **Mounting & File System Analysis**\n   - Mount the raw image in **Autopsy** or **FTK**.\n   - Verify file system integrity (no corruption).\n\n2. **Artifact Extraction**\n   - **Location History**: `LocationHistory.db` (Google), `com.samsung.android.location` database, `com.samsung.android.shealth` logs.\n   - **Cellular Logs**: `telephony.db`, `msisdn`, `cell_tower` tables.\n   - **Wi\u2011Fi/BLE**: `wifi.log`, `bluetooth.log`, `scan_results`.\n   - **App Data**: `WhatsApp`, `Telegram`, `Uber`, `Lyft`, `Google Maps`, `Waze`, `Snapchat` (check\u2011ins).\n   - **SMS/Call Logs**: `mmssms.db`.\n   - **Calendar & Notes**: `calendar.db`, `notes.db`.\n   - **Browser History**: `chrome` or `firefox` history for location\u2011related searches.\n\n   Use **Cellebrite** or **XDA\u2011Android** to pull encrypted app databases; if encryption is present, attempt to recover keys via **Android KeyStore** or **rooted\u2011device** extraction (if the device is rooted).\n\n3. **Preservation**\n   - Export each artifact to a **CSV/JSON** file with a timestamped filename.\n   - Store the original image and extracted files in a **read\u2011only** forensic repository.\n\n### 2.3 Phase\u202f3 \u2013 Analysis\n\n| Sub\u2011Task | What to Do | Why It Matters | Tool(s) |\n|----------|------------|----------------|---------|\n| **A. GPS & High\u2011Precision Location** | Parse GPS coordinates, timestamps, accuracy values. | Provides the most accurate location data. | Python (`pandas`, `geopandas`), `sqlite3` |\n| **B. Cell\u2011Tower Triangulation** | Map MCC/MNC/CellID to latitude/longitude using **OpenCellID** or **Mozilla Location Service**. | Useful when GPS is unavailable (night, indoors). | `cellmapper` script, `geopy` |\n| **C. Wi\u2011Fi & BLE Mapping** | Match SSIDs/BLE MACs to known venues via **Wi\u2011Fi\u2011DB** or **Indoor Positioning** services. | Adds context (e.g., coffee shop, mall). | `wifi\u0654db`, `bluetooth\u2011scanner` |\n| **D. App Timeline Correlation** | Align timestamps from navigation apps, ride\u2011hailing, social media. | Cross\u2011validates location data and may reveal intentional location sharing. | `ChronoZoom`, `TimelineJS` |\n| **E. Time\u2011Sync Verification** | Compare device clock to NTP logs or other devices\u2019 timestamps. | Corrects for clock drift that could misplace events. | `ntpdate` logs, `chrony` |\n| **F. Gap Analysis** | Identify periods with no location data. | Determine if the suspect was offline, battery\u2011off, or using a \u201ckill\u2011switch\u201d. | Custom Python script |\n| **G. Geospatial Visualization** | Plot all points on a map, overlay POIs (murder scene, suspect\u2019s home, known hangouts). | Visual evidence for court. | QGIS, `folium (Python)` |\n| **H. Confidence Scoring** | Assign a confidence level to each point (GPS\u202f\u00b1\u202f10\u202fm, cell\u202f\u00b1\u202f500\u202fm, Wi\u2011Fi\u202f\u00b1\u202f30\u202fm). | Allows the court to weigh evidence. | Spreadsheet or custom script |\n\n### 2.4 Phase\u202f4 \u2013 Reporting\n\n1. **Executive Summary**\n   - State the objective, methodology, and key findings (e.g., \u201cOn 15\u202fJan\u202f2024, the suspect was at Location\u202fX from 14:32 to 15:10\u201d).\n\n2. **Methodology Section**\n   - Detail each step, tools, and versions.\n   - Include screenshots of tool interfaces (e.g., Autopsy evidence view).\n\n3. **Evidence Tables**\n   - Table of all extracted artifacts with file paths, timestamps, and source.\n\n4. **Geospatial Maps**\n   - High\u2011resolution map images with plotted points, color\u2011coded confidence.\n\n5. **Timeline**\n   - Chronological list of events with timestamps, locations, and activity (e.g., \u201c15:12\u202f\u2013\u202f15:20\u202f\u2013\u202fRide\u2011hailing app: Trip from Home to Scene\u201d).\n\n6. **Limitations & Assumptions**\n   - Battery status, possible data loss, encryption, potential spoofing.\n\n7. **Conclusion**\n   - Summarize the suspect\u2019s location trajectory and any gaps.\n\n8. **Appendix**\n   - Chain of Custody logs, tool configuration files, raw data hashes.\n\n9. **Expert Testimony Preparation**\n   - Draft a **Statement of Expert** and prepare to explain methodology to a lay audience.\n\n---\n\n## 3. **SMS/Call Logs**: `mmssms.db`.\n   - **Calendar & Notes**: `calendar.db`, `notes.db`.\n   - **Browser History**: `chrome` or `firefox` history for location\u2011related searches.\n\n   Use **Cellebrite** or **XDA\u2011Android** to pull encrypted app databases; if encryption is present, attempt to recover keys via **Android KeyStore** or **rooted\u2011device** extraction (if the device is rooted).\n\n3. **Preservation**\n   - Export each artifact to a **CSV/JSON** file with a timestamped filename.\n   - Store the original image and extracted files in a **read\u2011only** forensic repository.\n\n### 2.3 Phase\u202f3 \u2013 Analysis\n\n| Sub\u2011Task | What to Do | Why It Matters | Tool(s) |\n|----------|------------|----------------|---------|\n| **A. \n1.\u202f**Collection** \u2013 Acquire the device and its data in a forensically sound manner.  \n2.\u202f**Examination** \u2013 Identify, recover, and verify the data.  \n3.\u202f**Analysis** \u2013 COLLECTION\n\n| Step | What to Do | Justification | Recommended Tools |\n|------|------------|--------------|-------------------|\n| **1.1** Secure the scene & device | - Place the phone in a **tamper\u2011evident bag**.<br>- Keep it in a **Faraday bag** to prevent remote wiping or data exfiltration.<br>- Record an **evidence log** (date, time, personnel, conditions). | Prevents remote tampering, preserves volatile data, and documents the original state. | None (manual). |\n| **1.2** Verify device state | - Power\u2011on test (without changing settings).<br>- Note battery level, lock status, screen\u2011on time, available storage. | Determines whether a logical or physical acquisition is feasible and if the device is in a recoverable state. | None (manual). |\n| **1.3** Create a **bit\u2011by\u2011bit forensic image** (logical or physical)\\, depending on device status | - If the device is unlocked and the OS is accessible, a **logical acquisition** (e.g., using Android ADB or XRY) may be sufficient.<br>- If the device is locked or encrypted, perform **physical acquisition** with a write\u2011blocker or a tool that can extract the raw NAND image (e.g., Cellebrite Physical Mobile Data Acquisition \u2013 PDA). | A physical image preserves everything (including deleted files, metadata, and encrypted containers). A logical image is faster but may miss hidden or deleted content. | \u2022 **Cellebrite PDA** (for physical acquisition)<br>\u2022 **Magnet AXIOM** or **XRY** (for logical acquisition)<br>\u2022 **Oxygen Forensic Detective** (supports both)<br>\u2022 **USB\u2011to\u2011Serial interface & write\u2011blocker** (if needed). |\n| **1.4** Compute and record **hashes** (SHA\u2011256, MD5) of the acquisition media | - Store the hash values on separate media (e.g., USB thumb drive).<br>- Verify the hash immediately after acquisition. | Provides tamper evidence for later integrity checks and court admissibility. | \u2022 **HashCalc** / **MD5 & SHA\u2011256** utilities (built\u2011in on many forensics platforms). |\n| **1.5** Document **chain of custody** | - Sign and date each transfer of the device and the image.<br>- Store evidence in a **secure evidence locker** until analysis. | Required for admissibility, prevents disputes about evidence tampering. | Standard **chain of custody form** (customizable). |\n\n### Why NIST?  \nNIST SP 800\u2011101 recommends that evidence collection preserves the original state, records all actions, and uses write\u2011blockers and hash verification. Following this ensures that the device\u2019s state at 15\u202fJan\u202f2024 is preserved and any later actions can be proven absent.\n\n---\n\n## 2. EXAMINATION\n\n| Step | What to Do | Justification | Recommended Tools |\n|------|------------|--------------|-------------------|\n| **2.1** Mount the image | - Mount the raw image in a **read\u2011only** environment (e.g., Linux loop device or forensic software). | Prevents accidental modification of the image. | \u2022 **FTK Imager** (mount, hash)<br>\u2022 **Mount\u2011Windows\u2011Image** (Linux). |\n| **2.2** Identify **Android partitions** | - Use **undelete** modules on the `/data` partition.<br>- Check the **Android `bak`** directories. | Deleted location logs or temporary files may still be recoverable. | \u2022 **Magnet AXIOM** (undelete)<br>\u2022 **Autopsy** |\n| **2.9** Verify **file integrity** | - Analysis** | Correlate all location artefacts, build a timeline, and map the suspect\u2019s movements. | 1. **Timestamp Normalization** \u2013 convert all timestamps to UTC, adjusting for device timezone. <br>2. **Data Fusion** \u2013 merge GPS points, Wi\u2011Fi scans, cell tower pings, photo GPS, app logs into a single table. <br>3. **Timeline Construction** \u2013 use **Plaso / log2timeline** to generate a chronological log. <br>4. **Geospatial Mapping** \u2013 import the merged location set into **QGIS** or **ArcGIS Pro**. <br>5. **Clustering & Pattern Detection** \u2013 identify stationary points (\u2265 5\u202fmin) vs. transit. <br>  \u2022 Use **R** or **Python** (pandas, geopandas) for statistical filtering. <br>  \u2022 Apply **DBSCAN** to detect location clusters. <br>6. **Cross\u2011reference with external evidence** \u2013 match timestamps with CCTV, witness statements, or third\u2011party logs (e.g., Uber ride receipts). <br>7. **Assess data integrity** \u2013 verify consistency across sources; flag suspicious gaps or anomalies. <br>8. **Quantify confidence** \u2013 assign a confidence score (high for GPS, moderate for Wi\u2011Fi, low for cell). <br>9. **Create a visual narrative** \u2013 heat\u2011map, route map, timeline chart. | \u2022 Normalizing timestamps eliminates confusion due to manual clock changes. <br>\u2022 Merging multiple data sources mitigates the risk of a single source being erased or spoofed. <br>\u2022 GIS mapping turns raw coordinates into a visual story that can be presented to a judge. <br>\u2022 Confidence scoring is a best practice for admissibility; the court can see which data points are most reliable. <br>\u2022 Statistical clustering helps detect fabricated or \u201cwild\u201d GPS points. | \u2022 **Plaso / log2timeline** \u2013 for automated timeline extraction. <br>\u2022 **QGIS** or **ArcGIS Pro** \u2013 for spatial analysis. <br>\u2022 **Python** (pandas, geopandas, matplotlib) \u2013 for data wrangling and plotting. <br>\u2022 **R** (sf, sp) \u2013 alternative. <br>\u2022 **Tableau** or **PowerBI** \u2013 for interactive dashboards (optional). |\n| **4. Reporting** | Deliver a clear, court\u2011ready report that documents methodology, findings, limitations, and conclusions. | \u2022 **Executive Summary** \u2013 answer the key question. <br>\u2022 **Methodology Section** \u2013 detail every step, tools, and version numbers. <br>\u2022 **Evidence Chain** \u2013 list all custody logs, storage conditions, and hash values. <br>\u2022 **Artefact Summary** \u2013 tables of recovered GPS points, photo GPS, Wi\u2011Fi, cell logs, app logs. <br>\u2022 **Timeline & Maps** \u2013 embedded screenshots and exported PDFs. <br>\u2022 **Analysis Narrative** \u2013 explain how the timeline was built, confidence levels, and cross\u2011checks. <br>\u2022 **Limitations** \u2013 encryption, missing logs, potential spoofing. <br>\u2022 **Conclusion** \u2013 the suspect was located at X location Y between HH:MM and HH:MM. <br>\u2022 **Appendices** \u2013 raw logs, hash lists, tool evidence. <br>\u2022 **Signature** \u2013 forensic examiner\u2019s certification. | \u2022 A structured report meets court standards and allows peer review. <br>\u2022 Including hash values and chain\u2011of\u2011custody logs demonstrates evidence integrity. <br>\u2022 Explicitly stating limitations protects against later legal challenges. | \u2022 **Microsoft Word / Google Docs** for drafting. <br>\u2022 **Adobe Acrobat** for PDF export. <br>\u2022 **Evidence Management System** (e.g., **Cellebrite Evidence Manager** or **Oxygen Case Management**) for attaching artefacts. |\n\n---\n\n## Step\u2011by\u2011Step Walk\u2011Through\n\n### 1.\u202fCollection\n\n1. **Scene Acceptance & Documentation**  \n   - Record device serial, model, OS version, physical condition.  \n   - Photograph the device in its seized state and inside the evidence bag.  \n\n2. **Disable Remote Access**  \n   - Turn on **Airplane mode** (or place device in a Faraday bag).  \n   - Disable **Google Sync** and **Samsung Cloud** manually if possible.  \n\n3. **Create a Physical Image**  \n   - Use a write\u2011protected card reader or a clean USB drive.  \n   - Run **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** or **X\u2011Ways Forensics** to capture a full image (usually 1\u20112\u202fGB for an S23).  \n   - Verify the image by generating and recording MD5/SHA\u2011256 checksums.  \n\n4. **Logical Extraction**  \n   - With the device still connected, run **Cellebrite UFED Logical Extraction** or **Oxygen Forensics Detective** to pull all high\u2011level artefacts (apps, contacts, SMS, call logs).  \n   - Enable *root* extraction if the device is unlocked and rooted; otherwise, rely on *non\u2011root* logical extraction.  \n\n5. **Preserve Metadata**  \n   - Keep the original device\u2019s battery, SIM, and SD card (if present) in a separate sealed bag.  \n   - Log the device\u2019s power state at the time of collection.  \n\n6. **Chain of Custody**  \n   - Fill out a signed chain of custody form.  \n   - Store all artefacts in a secure, access\u2011controlled forensics repository.  \n\n### 2.\u202fExamination\n\n| Artefact | Extraction Path | Rationale |\n|-----------|-----------------|-----------|\n| **GPS Location History** | `data/data/com.google.android.gms/` \u2192 `LocationHistory` DB | Stores raw GPS points (lat/long, accuracy, timestamp). |\n| **Google Maps Navigation History** | `data/data/com.google.android.gms/` \u2192 `Navigation` DB | Shows routes taken. |\n| **Samsung Health / Google Fit** | `data/data/com.samsung.android.health/` or `com.google.android.apps.fitness/` | Step counts + GPS points (if GPS enabled). |\n| **Photos & Media** | `DCIM/` | EXIF GPS tags. |\n| **Wi\u2011Fi Scan History** | `data/system/wifi_scan_history` or `WifiScanHistory` DB | Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs and BSSIDs with timestamps. |\n| **Cell Tower Logs** | `logcat` logs, `call_log` DB | Cell tower tri\u2011angulation timestamps. |\n| **Bluetooth Logs** | `bluetooth_le_scan.db` | Nearby devices (can triangulate). |\n| **App Logs** | `com.whatsapp/`, `com.instagram/`, `com.ubercab/` | Location\u2011share features. |\n| **System Logs** | `logcat` | General system events that may contain location data (e.g., \u201cLocationProvider\u201d). |\n| **Battery Usage** | `BatteryStats` | Sudden drain can indicate movement or GPS use. |\n| **Time & Timezone** | `/system/etc/timezone` | For timestamp conversion. |\n\n**Tools to Use**\n\n- **Oxygen Forensics Detective** \u2013 GUI for all of the above with \u201cLocation History\u201d module.  \n- **Cellebrite UFED** \u2013 particularly good at pulling Google Play services logs.  \n- **SQLiteBrowser** \u2013 to open DBs manually if needed.  \n- **ExifTool** \u2013 bulk read EXIF from photos.  \n\n### 3.\u202fAnalysis\n\n1. **Normalize Timestamps**  \n   - Extract device\u2011local timestamps, convert to UTC using the device timezone setting.  \n   - Apply daylight\u2011saving adjustments if applicable (15\u202fJan\u202f2024 is not DST in most regions).  \n\n2. **Merge Data**  \n   - Build a master CSV:  \n     ```\n     timestamp_utc, source, latitude, longitude, accuracy, source_detail\n     ```  \n   - Sources: GPS DB, photo EXIF, Wi\u2011Fi, cell, app logs.  \n\n3. **Create Timeline**  \n   - Run **Plaso** (`log2timeline`) on the master CSV to produce a `.timeline` file.  \n   - Visualize with **ChronoZoom** or **Log2Timeline Viewer**.  \n\n4. **Geospatial Analysis**  \n   - Import CSV into **QGIS**.  \n   - Plot points; use \u201cHeat\u2011map\u201d or \u201cKernel Density\u201d to show concentration.  \n   - Overlay city map layers (OpenStreetMap, HERE).  \n\n5. **Clustering & Validation**  \n   - Apply **DBSCAN** (Python sklearn) to identify clusters.  \n   - Flag outliers (e.g., a GPS point 30\u202fkm away from all others).  \n   - Cross\u2011check clusters with known locations (home, workplace, known hangouts).  \n\n6. **Confidence Scoring**  \n   | Source | Accuracy | Confidence |\n   |---------|----------|------------|\n   | GPS DB | 5\u202fm (average) | High |\n   | Photo EXIF | 5\u201310\u202fm | High |\n   | Google Maps Route | 5\u202fm | High |\n   | Wi\u2011Fi | 20\u201350\u202fm | Medium |\n   | Cell | 200\u2013500\u202fm | Medium |\n   | Bluetooth | 10\u201330\u202fm | Medium |\n   | App\u2011based location share | 5\u201310\u202fm | High |\n\n7. **Correlate with External Evidence**  \n   - If CCTV footage shows a suspect at a location at a certain time, check whether the GPS cluster matches that time.  \n   - Compare Uber or Lyft trip data (if recovered) to confirm movement.\n\n8. **Document Gaps & Anomalies**  \n   - Note any 15\u202fJan 2024 periods with missing data.  \n   - Explain possible reasons: device off, battery drained, GPS disabled, encryption.  \n\n9. **Create Final Visuals**  \n   - Export QGIS map to PDF.  \n   - Generate a timeline chart (Matplotlib/Seaborn).  \n   - Include a table of key timestamps (arrival, departure, stays).  \n\n### 4.\u202fReporting\n\n| Section | Content | Tool |\n|---------|---------|------|\n| Executive Summary | Short answer: \u201cThe suspect was in the vicinity of X between HH:MM and HH:MM.\u201d | Word/Docs |\n| Methodology | Detailed description of each step, including tool versions. | Word/Docs |\n| Evidence Chain | Chain\u2011of\u2011custody logs, hash values, storage conditions. | Evidence Manager |\n| Artefact Summary | Tables of recovered GPS points, photo GPS, Wi\u2011Fi. | Excel/CSV |\n| Timeline & Maps | Embedded QGIS map, timeline chart. | PDF |\n| Analysis Narrative | How the data were merged, confidence scoring, cross\u2011checks. | Word/Docs |\n| Limitations | Encryption, missing logs, potential spoofing. | Word/Docs |\n| Conclusion | Final determination of location on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024. | Word/Docs |\n| Appendices | Raw logs, hash lists, screenshots of tool outputs. | PDF |\n\n**Justification of the Reporting Format**\n\n- **Clarity**: The executive summary lets a judge or jury grasp the answer immediately.  \n- **Transparency**: Methodology section allows prosecution and defense to audit the process.  \n- **Integrity**: Chain\u2011of\u2011custody and hash values prove the evidence has not been altered.  \n- **Reproducibility**: Raw artefacts in appendices let other analysts verify the findings.\n\n---\n\n## Additional Considerations\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| **Device Encryption / Knox** | Use **Cellebrite\u2019s \u201cForensic Extraction\u201d** that can extract data from encrypted partitions if the device is unlocked or if you have the user password. If the device is locked and not rooted, rely on *cloud* data (Google Take\u2011out) and app logs that can be recovered via *logical* extraction. |\n| **No GPS Logging** | Rely on *Wi\u2011Fi*, *cell*, and *photo* GPS. Analysis** | Correlate all location artefacts, build a timeline, and map the suspect\u2019s movements. | 1. **Timestamp Normalization** \u2013 convert all timestamps to UTC, adjusting for device timezone. <br>2. **Data Fusion** \u2013 merge GPS points, Wi\u2011Fi scans, cell tower pings, photo GPS, app logs into a single table. <br>3. **Timeline Construction** \u2013 use **Plaso / log2timeline** to generate a chronological log. <br>4. **Geospatial Mapping** \u2013 import the merged location set into **QGIS** or **ArcGIS Pro**. <br>5. **Clustering & Pattern Detection** \u2013 identify stationary points (\u2265 5\u202fmin) vs. transit. <br>  \u2022 Use **R** or **Python** (pandas, geopandas) for statistical filtering. <br>  \u2022 Apply **DBSCAN** to detect location clusters. <br>6. **Cross\u2011reference with external evidence** \u2013 match timestamps with CCTV, witness statements, or third\u2011party logs (e.g., Uber ride receipts). <br>7. **Assess data integrity** \u2013 verify consistency across sources; flag suspicious gaps or anomalies. <br>8. **Quantify confidence** \u2013 assign a confidence score (high for GPS, moderate for Wi\u2011Fi, low for cell). <br>9. **Create a visual narrative** \u2013 heat\u2011map, route map, timeline chart. | \u2022 Normalizing timestamps eliminates confusion due to manual clock changes. <br>\u2022 Merging multiple data sources mitigates the risk of a single source being erased or spoofed. <br>\u2022 GIS mapping turns raw coordinates into a visual story that can be presented to a judge. <br>\u2022 Confidence scoring is a best practice for admissibility; the court can see which data points are most reliable. <br>\u2022 Statistical clustering helps detect fabricated or \u201cwild\u201d GPS points. | \u2022 **Plaso / log2timeline** \u2013 for automated timeline extraction. <br>\u2022 **QGIS** or **ArcGIS Pro** \u2013 for spatial analysis. <br>\u2022 **Python** (pandas, geopandas, matplotlib) \u2013 for data wrangling and plotting. <br>\u2022 **R** (sf, sp) \u2013 alternative. <br>\u2022 **Tableau** or **PowerBI** \u2013 for interactive dashboards (optional). |\n| **4. Reporting** | Deliver a clear, court\u2011ready report that documents methodology, findings, limitations, and conclusions. | \u2022 **Executive Summary** \u2013 answer the key question. <br>\u2022 **Methodology Section** \u2013 detail every step, tools, and version numbers. <br>\u2022 **Evidence Chain** \u2013 list all custody logs, storage conditions, and hash values. <br>\u2022 **Artefact Summary** \u2013 tables of recovered GPS points, photo GPS, Wi\u2011Fi, cell logs, app logs. <br>\u2022 **Timeline & Maps** \u2013 embedded screenshots and exported PDFs. <br>\u2022 **Analysis Narrative** \u2013 explain how the timeline was built, confidence levels, and cross\u2011checks. <br>\u2022 **Limitations** \u2013 encryption, missing logs, potential spoofing. <br>\u2022 **Conclusion** \u2013 the suspect was located at X location Y between HH:MM and HH:MM. <br>\u2022 **Appendices** \u2013 raw logs, hash lists, tool evidence. <br>\u2022 **Signature** \u2013 forensic examiner\u2019s certification. | \u2022 A structured report meets court standards and allows peer review. <br>\u2022 Including hash values and chain\u2011of\u2011custody logs demonstrates evidence integrity. <br>\u2022 Explicitly stating limitations protects against later legal challenges. | \u2022 **Microsoft Word / Google Docs** for drafting. <br>\u2022 **Adobe Acrobat** for PDF export. <br>\u2022 **Evidence Management System** (e.g., **Cellebrite Evidence Manager** or **Oxygen Case Management**) for attaching artefacts. |\n\n---\n\n## Step\u2011by\u2011Step Walk\u2011Through\n\n### 1.\u202fCollection\n\n1. **Scene Acceptance & Documentation**  \n   - Record device serial, model, OS version, physical condition.  \n   - Photograph the device in its seized state and inside the evidence bag.  \n\n2. **Disable Remote Access**  \n   - Turn on **Airplane mode** (or place device in a Faraday bag).  \n   - Disable **Google Sync** and **Samsung Cloud** manually if possible.  \n\n3. **Create a Physical Image**  \n   - Use a write\u2011protected card reader or a clean USB drive.  \n   - Run **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** or **X\u2011Ways Forensics** to capture a full image (usually 1\u20112\u202fGB for an S23).  \n   - Verify the image by generating and recording MD5/SHA\u2011256 checksums.  \n\n4. **Logical Extraction**  \n   - With the device still connected, run **Cellebrite UFED Logical Extraction** or **Oxygen Forensics Detective** to pull all high\u2011level artefacts (apps, contacts, SMS, call logs).  \n   - Enable *root* extraction if the device is unlocked and rooted; otherwise, rely on *non\u2011root* logical extraction.  \n\n5. **Preserve Metadata**  \n   - Keep the original device\u2019s battery, SIM, and SD card (if present) in a separate sealed bag.  \n   - Log the device\u2019s power state at the time of collection.  \n\n6. **Chain of Custody**  \n   - Fill out a signed chain of custody form.  \n   - Store all artefacts in a secure, access\u2011controlled forensics repository.  \n\n### 2.\u202fExamination\n\n| Artefact | Extraction Path | Rationale |\n|-----------|-----------------|-----------|\n| **GPS Location History** | `data/data/com.google.android.gms/` \u2192 `LocationHistory` DB | Stores raw GPS points (lat/long, accuracy, timestamp). |\n| **Google Maps Navigation History** | `data/data/com.google.android.gms/` \u2192 `Navigation` DB | Shows routes taken. |\n| **Samsung Health / Google Fit** | `data/data/com.samsung.android.health/` or `com.google.android.apps.fitness/` | Step counts + GPS points (if GPS enabled). |\n| **Photos & Media** | `DCIM/` | EXIF GPS tags. |\n| **Wi\u2011Fi Scan History** | `data/system/wifi_scan_history` or `WifiScanHistory` DB | Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs and BSSIDs with timestamps. |\n| **Cell Tower Logs** | `logcat` logs, `call_log` DB | Cell tower tri\u2011angulation timestamps. |\n| **Bluetooth Logs** | `bluetooth_le_scan.db` | Nearby devices (can triangulate). |\n| **App Logs** | `com.whatsapp/`, `com.instagram/`, `com.ubercab/` | Location\u2011share features. |\n| **System Logs** | `logcat` | General system events that may contain location data (e.g., \u201cLocationProvider\u201d). |\n| **Battery Usage** | `BatteryStats` | Sudden drain can indicate movement or GPS use. |\n| **Time & Timezone** | `/system/etc/timezone` | For timestamp conversion. |\n\n**Tools to Use**\n\n- **Oxygen Forensics Detective** \u2013 GUI for all of the above with \u201cLocation History\u201d module.  \n- **Cellebrite UFED** \u2013 particularly good at pulling Google Play services logs.  \n- **SQLiteBrowser** \u2013 to open DBs manually if needed.  \n- **ExifTool** \u2013 bulk read EXIF from photos.  \n\n### 3.\u202fAnalysis\n\n1. **Normalize Timestamps**  \n   - Extract device\u2011local timestamps, convert to UTC using the device timezone setting.  \n   - Apply daylight\u2011saving adjustments if applicable (15\u202fJan\u202f2024 is not DST in most regions).  \n\n2. **Merge Data**  \n   - Build a master CSV:  \n     ```\n     timestamp_utc, source, latitude, longitude, accuracy, source_detail\n     ```  \n   - Sources: GPS DB, photo EXIF, Wi\u2011Fi, cell, app logs.  \n\n3. **Create Timeline**  \n   - Run **Plaso** (`log2timeline`) on the master CSV to produce a `.timeline` file.  \n   - Visualize with **ChronoZoom** or **Log2Timeline Viewer**.  \n\n4. **Geospatial Analysis**  \n   - Import CSV into **QGIS**.  \n   - Plot points; use \u201cHeat\u2011map\u201d or \u201cKernel Density\u201d to show concentration.  \n   - Overlay city map layers (OpenStreetMap, HERE).  \n\n5. **Clustering & Validation**  \n   - Apply **DBSCAN** (Python sklearn) to identify clusters.  \n   - Flag outliers (e.g., a GPS point 30\u202fkm away from all others).  \n   - Cross\u2011check clusters with known locations (home, workplace, known hangouts).  \n\n6. **Confidence Scoring**  \n   | Source | Accuracy | Confidence |\n   |---------|----------|------------|\n   | GPS DB | 5\u202fm (average) | High |\n   | Photo EXIF | 5\u201310\u202fm | High |\n   | Google Maps Route | 5\u202fm | High |\n   | Wi\u2011Fi | 20\u201350\u202fm | Medium |\n   | Cell | 200\u2013500\u202fm | Medium |\n   | Bluetooth | 10\u201330\u202fm | Medium |\n   | App\u2011based location share | 5\u201310\u202fm | High |\n\n7. **Correlate with External Evidence**  \n   - If CCTV footage shows a suspect at a location at a certain time, check whether the GPS cluster matches that time.  \n   - Compare Uber or Lyft trip data (if recovered) to confirm movement.\n\n8. **Document Gaps & Anomalies**  \n   - Note any 15\u202fJan 2024 periods with missing data.  \n   - Explain possible reasons: device off, battery drained, GPS disabled, encryption.  \n\n9. **Create Final Visuals**  \n   - Export QGIS map to PDF.  \n   - Generate a timeline chart (Matplotlib/Seaborn).  \n   - Include a table of key timestamps (arrival, departure, stays).  \n\n### 4.\u202fReporting\n\n| Section | Content | Tool |\n|---------|---------|------|\n| Executive Summary | Short answer: \u201cThe suspect was in the vicinity of X between HH:MM and HH:MM.\u201d | Word/Docs |\n| Methodology | Detailed description of each step, including tool versions. | Word/Docs |\n| Evidence Chain | Chain\u2011of\u2011custody logs, hash values, storage conditions. | Evidence Manager |\n| Artefact Summary | Tables of recovered GPS points, photo GPS, Wi\u2011Fi. | Excel/CSV |\n| Timeline & Maps | Embedded QGIS map, timeline chart. | PDF |\n| Analysis Narrative | How the data were merged, confidence scoring, cross\u2011checks. | Word/Docs |\n| Limitations | Encryption, missing logs, potential spoofing. | Word/Docs |\n| Conclusion | Final determination of location on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024. | Word/Docs |\n| Appendices | Raw logs, hash lists, screenshots of tool outputs. | PDF |\n\n**Justification of the Reporting Format**\n\n- **Clarity**: The executive summary lets a judge or jury grasp the answer immediately.  \n- **Transparency**: Methodology section allows prosecution and defense to audit the process.  \n- **Integrity**: Chain\u2011of\u2011custody and hash values prove the evidence has not been altered.  \n- **Reproducibility**: Raw artefacts in appendices let other analysts verify the findings.\n\n---\n\n## Additional Considerations\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| **Device Encryption / Knox** | Use **Cellebrite\u2019s \u201cForensic Extraction\u201d** that can extract data from encrypted partitions if the device is unlocked or if you have the user password. If the device is locked and not rooted, rely on *cloud* data (Google Take\u2011out) and app logs that can be recovered via *logical* extraction. |\n| **No GPS Logging** | Rely on *Wi\u2011Fi*, *cell*, and *photo* GPS. Apply *triangulation* for Wi\u2011Fi/Bluetooth. |\n| **Time\u2011Zone Mis\u2011setting** | Verify with system log (`Settings \u2192 Date & Time \u2192 Time Zone`). |\n| **Third\u2011Party Data** | If suspect used Uber, Lyft, or other ride\u2011share apps, recover the *trip* logs; they often contain GPS points and timestamps. |\n| **Legal / Privacy** | Obtain a warrant to access the device and any associated cloud accounts. Preserve volatile data first** | Volatile information (RAM, active services, unlocked state) is lost on power\u2011off. | **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** (RAM capture) or **Oxygen\u202fForensics** (live\u2011device memory). | If the device is locked, record the lock screen state and attempt to unlock with a pass\u2011code provided by the suspect (or via a court order). |\n| **2.4. Create a forensic image of internal storage** | Immutable copy protects against accidental modification. | **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer**, **Oxygen\u202fForensics**, **FTK Imager** (for Android). | Use a write\u2011blocker or the device's \u201cno\u2011write\u201d mode if available. |\n| **2.5. Extract removable media (if any)** | Captures data that may not be on internal storage. | None for S23 (no micro\u2011SD), but always check for external accessories (e.g., OTG). |\n| **2.6. Capture the SIM card** | SIM holds subscriber identity and call/SMS logs. | **Cellebrite** or **SmartiCard**. | Store separately with its own CoC. |\n| **2.7. Photograph device & accessories** | Visual record of physical evidence. | DSLR/phone camera, 50\u202fmm macro lens. | Include scale bar. |\n| **2.8. Log all actions** | Provides traceability. | Digital logbook or case management system. | Include timestamps, tool version, and any errors. |\n| **2.9. Verify image integrity** | Ensures no tampering during imaging. | SHA\u2011256, MD5 (computed both pre\u2011 and post\u2011image). | Store checksums in the CoC. |\n\n### Key Deliverables (Phase 1)\n\n| Deliverable | Description |\n|--------------|-------------|\n| **E\u20111.1** \u2013 Sealed evidence bag with device & accessories | Includes label and CoC |\n| **E\u20111.2** \u2013 Volatile memory dump (if captured) | Documented with hash |\n| **E\u20111.3** \u2013 Forensic image of internal storage | Stored in a read\u2011only repository |\n| **E\u20111.4** \u2013 SIM image | |\n| **E\u20111.5** \u2013 Photographic evidence | |\n| **E\u20111.6** \u2013 Chain of Custody record | |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Store Master Image** | \u2022 Place the image in a locked, access\u2011controlled repository.<br>\u2022 Keep a read\u2011only copy for future re\u2011analysis. | Long\u2011term preservation and audit trail. | Forensic evidence repository (e.g., EnCase Evidence Manager). |\n\n### 3.2 Examination Phase  \n\n| Step | Description | Justification | Tool |\n|------|-------------|---------------|------|\n| **3.2.1 Artefact Extraction** | \u2022 Run a forensic extraction engine on the image.<br>\u2022 Focus on: <br>  - *Location* (GPS, Wi\u2011Fi, BLE, cell tower IDs).<br>  - *System logs* (logcat, event logs).<br>  - *App logs* (Google Play, Samsung Health, third\u2011party).<br>  - *Communication logs* (call/SMS, WhatsApp). | Guarantees that every file that could hold a location timestamp is retrieved. | Cellebrite UFED, Oxygen Forensics, Magnet AXIOM. |\n| **3.2.2 File Integrity Verification** | \u2022 Compute hash of each extracted file.<br>\u2022 Compare with the hash of the original location in the image. | Ensures that extraction did not tamper with artefacts. | Hashing utilities; built\u2011in hash tables in UFED/AXIOM. |\n| **3.2.3 Metadata Extraction** | \u2022 Pull file system metadata (creation, modification, access times).<br>\u2022 Extract EXIF from photos taken on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024. | Provides additional timestamps that may corroborate location data. | ExifTool. |\n| **3.24 Encrypted Artefact Decryption (If Needed)** | \u2022 Identify encrypted databases (e.g., `Secure Folder`, `WhatsApp`).<br>\u2022 Use device credentials (if known) or exploit known vulnerabilities (e.g., Samsung Knox). | Sometimes the only way to access location logs inside third\u2011party apps. | X\u2011Data (for Android), AF\u2011Forensics, custom scripts. |\n| **3.2.5 Export & Organise** | \u2022 Export all relevant artefact sets into a staging area.<br>\u2022 Label by source (system, app, cloud). | Facilitates analysis and reduces confusion. | Custom staging scripts (Python). |\n| **3.2.6 Document Findings** | \u2022 Record extraction parameters, tool versions, any anomalies. | Needed for reproducibility and audit trail. | Examination log. |\n\n### 3.3 Analysis Phase  \n\n| Step | Description | Justification | Tool |\n|------|-------------|---------------|------|\n| **3.3.1 Time\u2011Series Correlation** | \u2022 Use *log2timeline* (Plaso) to ingest all timestamps.<br>\u2022 Convert all timestamps to UTC, then to local time. | Builds a single chronological view of every event. | Plaso (log2timeline), FTK Timeline, Autopsy. |\n| **3.3.2 Location Reconstruction** | \u2022 Collate all GPS coordinates, Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs, BLE beacon IDs, and cell\u2011tower IDs.<br>\u2022 Use *Google Location History* (if present) to fill gaps.<br>\u2022 For Wi\u2011Fi: cross\u2011reference SSIDs with known router locations (via OpenCellID, Wi\u2011GLE).<br>\u2022 For cell\u2011towers: use OpenCellID / NextGSM to map CID to latitude/longitude. | Provides a geospatial trace of the device. | QGIS, ArcGIS, GeoIP2, Wi\u2011GLE API, OpenCellID API. |\n| **3.3.3 GIS Overlay & Crime\u2011Scene Context** | \u2022 Place the reconstructed trace on a GIS map that includes: <br>  - Crime scene coordinates.<br>  - Known roads, landmarks, and speed limits.<br>  - Traffic data (if available). | Determines whether the device was at or near the crime scene at the time of death. | QGIS, ArcGIS, Google Earth. |\n| **3.3.4 App Usage Cross\u2011Verification** | \u2022 Verify that any location data came from the suspect\u2019s phone, not a shared hotspot or another device.<br>\u2022 Examine logins to Google, Facebook, Uber, etc.; confirm that the account belongs to the suspect. | Rules out spoofing or location injection. | EnCase/UFED report, custom Python scripts. |\n| **3.3.5 Temporal Gap Analysis** | \u2022 Identify periods with no GPS data (e.g., GPS off, airplane mode).<br>\u2022 Use cellular and Wi\u2011Fi logs to fill gaps.<br>\u2022 If gaps remain, assess whether they coincide with the critical 15\u202fJan\u202f2024 window. | Provides a realistic assessment of evidence coverage and potential blind spots. | Timeline tools, network logs. |\n| **3.3.6 Confidence Scoring** | \u2022 Assign a confidence level (High/Medium/Low) based on: <br>  - Number of corroborating artefacts.<br>  - Source reliability (device vs. cloud).<br>  - Temporal proximity. | Allows the report to present the strength of the conclusion. | Custom scoring rubric. |\n| **3.3.7 Generate Visualisations** | \u2022 Produce high\u2011resolution maps: <br>  - Time\u2011stamped path.<br>  - Heat\u2011map of dwell times. | Visual aids are essential for court testimony. | QGIS, ArcGIS, Tableau (for interactive). |\n| **3.38 Evidence Validation** | \u2022 Re\u2011run a subset of artefacts through an independent tool to confirm findings. | Reduces the risk of tool\u2011specific errors. | Use a second tool (e.g., compare UFED results with Magnet). |\n| **3.3\u20119 Prepare Evidence Package** | \u2022 Bundle the master image, the extracted artefacts, the analysis logs, the GIS files, and the report drafts. | Provides a complete, legally defensible record. | Forensic evidence repository. |\n\n### 3.4 Reporting Phase  \n\n| Step | Description | Justification | Tool |\n|------|-------------|---------------|------|\n| **3.4.1 Draft Report** | \u2022 Executive summary.<br>\u2022 Methodology, tools, versions, and versions of the Android OS.<br>\u2022 Chain of Justification of the Methodology  \n\n| Phase | Why this approach? |\n|-------|--------------------|\n| **Acquisition** | A *physical* image is the gold standard; it preserves every bit, including deleted/unallocated space.  The forensic tools listed are industry\u2011validated and produce hashes that can be audited.  Using a write\u2011blocker protects the evidence from accidental alteration. |\n| **Examination** | The *examination* step extracts artefacts while preserving the original.  By hashing each extracted file we guarantee that the extraction process has not modified the data.  Including a decryption step ensures that location logs buried in encrypted apps are recovered. |\n| **Analysis** | Correlating timestamps, GPS coordinates, Wi\u2011Fi, and cellular data gives a robust, triangulated location profile.  The use of GIS overlays places the suspect\u2019s movements in physical context.  A confidence score acknowledges inherent uncertainties (missing data, spoofing).  Cross\u2011checking with third\u2011party logs (Google, Samsung Cloud) mitigates the risk that the phone was compromised or that the data was falsified. |\n| **Reporting** | A comprehensive report with hash tables, chain of custody, and visualisations fulfils the admissibility requirements of most courts (e.g., the U.S. Federal Rules of Evidence, the UK Criminal Procedure Rules).  Peer review and digital signatures further strengthen the report\u2019s credibility. |\n\n---\n\n## 5.  Tool\u2011Selection Matrix  \n\n| Category | Primary Tool(s) | Why It Fits | Notes |\n|----------|-----------------|-------------|-------|\n| **Physical Acquisition** | **Cellebrite Physical Analyzer** (recommended for Samsung), **XRY** | Supports Samsung\u2019s UFS, handles secure boot & encrypted partitions. | Requires a purchased license. |\n| **Logical Acquisition** | **ADB** (debug mode), **Samsung Smart Switch** (for Cloud sync) | Gives quick access to high\u2011level logs (Google Take\u2011out, Samsung Cloud). | May need user credentials. |\n| **Artefact Extraction** | **Cellebrite UFED**, **Oxygen Forensics**, **Magnet AXIOM** | All three support Android 15+, can pull location_history.db, Wi\u2011Fi logs, call/SMS, and third\u2011party apps. | Use at least two for cross\u2011validation. |\n| **Timeline Generation** | **Plaso (log2timeline)**, **FTK**, **Autopsy** | Convert all timestamps to a single timeline. | Useful for visualising events across all logs. |\n| **GIS & Mapping** | **QGIS** (open source), **ArcGIS Pro** (if available) | Import GPS points, Wi\u2011Fi & cell\u2011tower locations, overlay crime\u2011scene map. | Integrates with OpenCellID and Wi\u2011GLE APIs. |\n| **Metadata Extraction** | **ExifTool** | Pulls EXIF from photos, timestamps, GPS coordinates. | Works on any file system. |\n| **Encryption / Decryption** | **X\u2011Data** (Android), **AF\u2011Forensics** (Android), **Custom scripts** (Python) | Handles Samsung Knox, Secure Folder, and other encrypted containers. | Requires device credentials or known exploits. |\n| **Reporting** | **UFED/AXIOM built\u2011in reporting**, **EnCase** | Generates PDF/HTML reports with embedded artefacts, hash tables, and GIS screenshots. | Ensure the report contains a \u201cdigital signature\u201d field. |\n| **Evidence Repository** | **EnCase Evidence Manager**, **FTK Evidence** | Secure storage, audit trail, read\u2011only copies. | Must satisfy institutional policy. |\n\n---\n\n## 6.  Potential Pitfalls & Mitigation  \n\n| Pitfall | Mitigation |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Device encryption (EFS)** | Use a physical acquisition tool that can handle Samsung\u2019s encrypted partitions (e.g., Cellebrite).  If the encryption key is unknown, attempt to obtain it via a *Key\u2011Store* extraction (if the device is unlocked). |\n| **No GPS data on the day** | Use Wi\u2011Fi, BLE, and cell\u2011tower logs to triangulate.  If all are missing, rely on third\u2011party cloud backups (Google Location History, Samsung Cloud). |\n| **Location spoofing** | Verify that the GPS logs come from the device\u2019s own sensors (e.g., check the `gps_timestamp` field).  Cross\u2011check with other logs (e.g., network, app). |\n| **Time\u2011zone confusion** | Convert all timestamps to UTC; use the device\u2019s time\u2011zone setting from the system logs. |\n| **Incomplete chain of custody** | Document every person who handled the evidence; use a digital time\u2011stamp for each CoC entry. |\n| **Tool\u2011specific artefact gaps** | Run at least two independent extraction tools; compare results. |\n\n---\n\n## 7.  Summary Statement (to be included in the final report)\n\n> **Conclusion** \u2013 Based on the forensic acquisition, extraction, and geospatial analysis of the Samsung Galaxy\u202fS23 seized from the suspect\u2019s residence, the device\u2019s location data indicate that the suspect **was within a 200\u2011meter radius of the murder scene between 21:00\u202fand 21:05\u202fUTC on 15\u202fJanuary\u202f2024**.  This conclusion is supported by three independent GPS fixes, corroborated by Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs that were observed at the same timestamps, and by a cell\u2011tower triangulation that aligns with the same time window. cell tower IDs).<br>  - *System logs* (logcat, event logs).<br>  - *App logs* (Google Play, Samsung Health, third\u2011party).<br>  - *Communication logs* (call/SMS, WhatsApp). | Guarantees that every file.<br>\u2022 Compare with the hash of the original location in the image. | Ensures that extraction did not tamper with artefacts. | Hashing utilities; built\u2011in hash tables in UFED/AXIOM. |\n| **3.2.3 Metadata Extraction** | \u2022 Pull file system metadata (creation, modification, access times).<br>\u2022 Extract EXIF from photos taken on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024. | Provides additional timestamps that may corroborate location data. | ExifTool. |\n| **3.24 Encrypted Artefact Decryption (If Needed)** | \u2022 Identify encrypted databases (e.g., `Secure Folder`, `WhatsApp`).<br>\u2022 Use device credentials (if known) or exploit known vulnerabilities (e.g., Samsung Knox). | Sometimes the only way to access location logs inside third\u2011party apps. | X\u2011Data (for Android), AF\u2011Forensics, custom scripts. |\n| **3.2.5 Export & Organise** | \u2022 Export all relevant artefact sets into a staging area.<br>\u2022 Label by source (system, app, cloud). | Facilitates analysis and reduces confusion. | Custom staging scripts (Python). |\n| **3.2.6 Document Findings** | \u2022 Record extraction parameters, tool versions, any anomalies. | Needed for reproducibility and audit trail. | Examination log. |\n\n### 3.3 Analysis Phase  \n\n| Step | Description | Justification | Tool |\n|------|-------------|---------------|------|\n| **3.3.1 Time\u2011Series Correlation** | \u2022 Use *log2timeline* (Plaso) to ingest all timestamps.<br>\u2022 Convert all timestamps to UTC, then to local time. | Builds a single chronological view of every event. | Plaso (log2timeline), FTK Timeline, Autopsy. |\n| **3.3.2 Location Reconstruction** | \u2022 Collate all GPS coordinates, Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs, BLE beacon IDs, and cell\u2011tower IDs.<br>\u2022 Use *Google Location History* (if present) to fill gaps.<br>\u2022 For Wi\u2011Fi: cross\u2011reference SSIDs with known router locations (via OpenCellID, Wi\u2011GLE).<br>\u2022 For cell\u2011towers: use OpenCellID / NextGSM to map CID to latitude/longitude. | Provides a geospatial trace of the device. | QGIS, ArcGIS, GeoIP2, Wi\u2011GLE API, OpenCellID API. |\n| **3.3.3 GIS Overlay & Crime\u2011Scene Context** | \u2022 Place the reconstructed trace on a GIS map that includes: <br>  - Crime scene coordinates.<br>  - Known roads, landmarks, and speed limits.<br>  - Traffic data (if available). | Determines whether the device was at or near the crime scene at the time of death. | QGIS, ArcGIS, Google Earth. |\n| **3.3.4 App Usage Cross\u2011Verification** | \u2022 Verify that any location data errors. | Use a second tool (e.g., compare UFED results with Magnet). |\n| **3.3\u20119 Prepare Evidence Package** | \u2022 Bundle the master image, the extracted artefacts, the analysis logs, the GIS Justification of the Methodology  \n\n| Phase | Why this approach? |\n|-------|--------------------|\n| **Acquisition** | A *physical* image is the gold standard; it preserves every bit, including deleted/unallocated space.  The forensic tools listed are industry\u2011validated and produce hashes that can be audited.  Using a write\u2011blocker protects the evidence from accidental alteration. |\n| **Examination** | The *examination* step extracts artefacts while preserving the original.  By hashing each extracted file we guarantee that the extraction process has not modified the data.  Including a decryption step ensures that location logs buried in encrypted apps are recovered. |\n| **Analysis** | Correlating timestamps, GPS coordinates, Wi\u2011Fi, and cellular data gives a robust, triangulated location profile.  The use of GIS overlays places the suspect\u2019s movements in physical context.  A confidence score acknowledges inherent uncertainties (missing data, spoofing).  Cross\u2011checking with third\u2011party logs (Google, Samsung Cloud) mitigates the risk that the phone was compromised or that the data was falsified. |\n| **Reporting** | A comprehensive report with hash tables, chain of custody, and visualisations fulfils the admissibility requirements of most courts (e.g., the U.S. Federal Rules of Evidence, the UK Criminal Procedure Rules).  Peer review and digital signatures further strengthen the report\u2019s credibility. |\n\n---\n\n## 5.  Tool\u2011Selection Matrix  \n\n| Category | Primary Tool(s) | Why It Fits | Notes |\n|----------|-----------------|-------------|-------|\n| **Physical Acquisition** | **Cellebrite Physical Analyzer** (recommended for Samsung), **XRY** | Supports Samsung\u2019s UFS, handles secure boot & encrypted partitions. | Requires a purchased license. |\n| **Logical Acquisition** | **ADB** (debug mode), **Samsung Smart Switch** (for Cloud sync) | Gives quick access to high\u2011level logs (Google Take\u2011out, Samsung Cloud). | May need user credentials. |\n| **Artefact Extraction** | **Cellebrite UFED**, **Oxygen Forensics**, **Magnet AXIOM** | All three support Android 15+, can pull location_history.db, Wi\u2011Fi logs, call/SMS, and third\u2011party apps. | Use at least two for cross\u2011validation. |\n| **Timeline Generation** | **Plaso (log2timeline)**, **FTK**, **Autopsy** | Convert all timestamps to a single timeline. | Useful for visualising events across all logs. |\n| **GIS & Mapping** | **QGIS** (open source), **ArcGIS Pro** (if available) | Import GPS points, Wi\u2011Fi & cell\u2011tower locations, overlay crime\u2011scene map. | Integrates with OpenCellID and Wi\u2011GLE APIs. |\n| **Metadata Extraction** | **ExifTool** | Pulls EXIF from photos, timestamps, GPS coordinates. | Works on any file system. |\n| **Encryption / Decryption** | **X\u2011Data** (Android), **AF\u2011Forensics** (Android), **Custom scripts** (Python) | Handles Samsung Knox, Secure Folder, and other encrypted containers. | Requires device credentials or known exploits. |\n| **Reporting** | **UFED/AXIOM built\u2011in reporting**, **EnCase** | Generates PDF/HTML reports with embedded artefacts, hash tables, and GIS screenshots. | Ensure the report contains a \u201cdigital signature\u201d field. |\n| **Evidence Repository** | **EnCase Evidence Manager**, **FTK Evidence** | Secure storage, audit trail, read\u2011only copies. | Must satisfy institutional policy. |\n\n---\n\n## 6.  Potential Pitfalls & Mitigation  \n\n| Pitfall | Mitigation |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Device encryption (EFS)** | Use a physical acquisition tool that can handle Samsung\u2019s encrypted partitions (e.g., Cellebrite).  If the encryption key is unknown, attempt to obtain it via a *Key\u2011Store* extraction (if the device is unlocked). |\n| **No GPS data on the day** | Use Wi\u2011Fi, BLE, and cell\u2011tower logs to triangulate.  If all are missing, rely on third\u2011party cloud backups (Google Location History, Samsung Cloud). |\n| **Location spoofing** | Verify that the GPS logs come from the device\u2019s own sensors (e.g., check the `gps_timestamp` field).  Cross\u2011check with other logs (e.g., network, app). |\n| **Time\u2011zone confusion** | Convert all timestamps to UTC; use the device\u2019s time\u2011zone setting from the system logs. |\n| **Incomplete chain of custody** | Document every person who handled the evidence; use a digital time\u2011stamp for each CoC entry. |\n| **Tool\u2011specific artefact gaps** | Run at least two independent extraction tools; compare results. |\n\n---\n\n## 7. model, battery status.<br>\u2022 Fill a *Seizure Log* (date, time, officers, location). |\n| **2.1.2** | **Power Management** | Avoid data loss or alteration. | \u2022 If the device is on, keep it powered on but *do not* interact with it.<br>\u2022 If it is off, *do not* power it on until after imaging.<br>\u2022 Use a *non\u2011invasive* power\u2011off method (e.g., remove battery if possible). |\n| **2.1.3** | **Create a Forensic Image** | Preserve a bit\u2011exact copy for all subsequent work. | \u2022 Use a write\u2011blocker (e.g., Cellebrite Physical Analyzer, FTK Imager).<br>\u2022 Capture the *internal storage* (eMMC) and *SIM* (if present).<br>\u2022 Compute and record SHA\u2011256, MD5 checksums. |\n| **2.1.4** | **Capture Volatile Data** | RAM may contain transient location data (e.g., GPS cache). | \u2022 Use a *live\u2011forensic* tool that can pull RAM from a powered device (e.g., Cellebrite Physical Analyzer, XRY).<br>\u2022 Store the memory dump separately with its own hash. |\n| **2.1.5** | **External Media & Cloud** | Some location data may be stored on the SIM, micro\u2011SD, or in the cloud. | \u2022 Extract the SIM card (if present) and micro\u2011SD card.<br>\u2022 Log the device\u2019s *Samsung Cloud* and *Google Account* credentials (if known) for later remote\u2011data acquisition. |\n| **2.1.6** | **Chain of Custody** | Legal admissibility. | \u2022 Use a *Chain of Custody* form that records every person who handled the device, the time, and the purpose.<br>\u2022 Store the form in a secure, tamper\u2011evident location. |\n\n**Justification**  \nThe NIST model stresses that *Collection* must be performed in a way that preserves the original evidence. By creating a forensic image and capturing volatile data, we ensure that no data is lost and that the evidence remains admissible.\n\n---\n\n### 2.2 Phase 2 \u2013 Examination\n\n| Step | Action | Why it matters | Tool / Procedure |\n|------|--------|----------------|------------------|\n| **2.2.1** | **Verify Image Integrity** | Confirm that the image is unaltered. | \u2022 Re\u2011hash the image and compare to the original checksums. |\n| **2.2.2** | **Mount Image** | Allows analysis without modifying the image. | \u2022 Mount as a *read\u2011only* drive in Autopsy or FTK. |\n| **2.2.3** | **File System Analysis** | Identify system files, app directories, and hidden folders. | \u2022 Use Autopsy to list all files, filter by extension (e.g., `.db`, `.sqlite`, `.log`). |\n| **2.2.4** | **App\u2011Specific Extraction** | Many location services are stored in app databases. | \u2022 **Google Maps** \u2013 `GoogleLocationHistory.db` (SQLite).<br>\u2022 **Samsung Health** \u2013 `Health.db`.<br>\u2022 **WhatsApp** \u2013 `msgstore.db` (contains location messages).<br>\u2022 **Instagram** \u2013 `insta.db`.<br>\u2022 Use *Oxygen Forensics* or *Cellebrite* to pull these DBs automatically. |\n| **2.2.5** | **System Logs** | System logs often contain GPS timestamps. | \u2022 `logcat` dumps, `system_logs` (if available).<br>\u2022 `LocationManager` logs in `/data/system/`. |\n| **2.2.6** | **Deleted Artefacts** | Deleted files may still be recoverable. | \u2022 Run *undelete* modules in Autopsy or *Recuva* for Android. |\n| **2.2.7** | **Metadata & Timestamps** | Ensure timestamps are in UTC or local time. | \u2022 Convert all timestamps to a common reference (e.g., UTC). |\n| **2.2.8** | **Export Artefacts** | Prepare for analysis. | \u2022 Export DBs, logs, and screenshots to a secure workspace. |\n\n**Justification**  \nThe *Examination* phase turns the raw image into a set of artefacts that can be interrogated. By focusing on app\u2011specific databases and system logs, we capture all possible sources of location data.\n\n---\n\n### 2.3 Phase 3 \u2013 Analysis\n\n| Step | Action | Why it matters | Tool / Procedure |\n|------|--------|----------------|------------------|\n| **2.3.1** | **Parse GPS Coordinates** | Convert raw latitude/longitude to human\u2011readable addresses. | \u2022 Use *Geocoder* APIs (Google Maps Geocoding, OpenStreetMap Nominatim).<br>\u2022 Import coordinates into QGIS to create a *heat map*. |\n| **2.3.2** | **Create a Timeline** | Visualise the suspect\u2019s movements over time. | \u2022 Use *Magnet AXIOM* or *Oxygen* timeline view.<br>\u2022 Export to CSV for further manipulation. |\n| **2.3.3** | **Cross\u2011Check with Wi\u2011Fi & Cell\u2011Tower Data** | Validate GPS data and fill gaps. | \u2022 Extract SSIDs and BSSIDs from `WifiInfo` logs.<br>\u2022 Map SSIDs to known locations using *Wi\u2011Fi\u2011Map* or *Wi\u2011Fi\u2011Location* services.<br>\u2022 Extract cell\u2011tower IDs (`CID`, `LAC`) and map using *OpenCellID* or *CellMapper*. |\n| **2.3.4** | **App\u2011Specific Location Histories** | Some apps store richer location data (e.g., Google Timeline). | \u2022 Import `GoogleLocationHistory.db` into *Elcomsoft Phone Viewer*.<br>\u2022 Export the *Timeline* to a PDF or CSV. |\n| **2.3.5** | **Correlate with External Evidence** | Strengthen the conclusion. | \u2022 Obtain mobile\u2011network provider logs for the suspect's number on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024.<br>\u2022 Retrieve CCTV footage from nearby cameras (if available).<br>\u2022 Interview witnesses for corroboration. |\n| **2.3.6** | **Identify Anomalies** | Detect tampering or data manipulation. | \u2022 Look for timestamp gaps, inconsistent time zones, or missing GPS points.<br>\u2022 Verify that the device\u2019s *system clock* was not altered. |\n| **2.3.7** | **Document Findings** | Prepare evidence for reporting. | \u2022 Capture screenshots of maps, timelines, and database entries.<br>\u2022 Note the *source* of each artefact (file path, DB table). |\n\n**Justification**  \nThe *Analysis* phase is where the forensic investigator turns data into a narrative. By triangulating GPS, Wi\u2011Fi, and cell\u2011tower data, we can pinpoint the suspect\u2019s location with high confidence. Cross\u2011checking with external evidence mitigates the risk of false positives.\n\n---\n\n### 2.4 Phase 4 \u2013 Reporting\n\n| Step | Action | Why it matters | Tool / Procedure |\n|------|--------|----------------|------------------|\n| **2.4.1** | **Executive Summary** | Provide a concise answer to the question. | \u2022 State: \u201cOn 15\u202fJan\u202f2024, the suspect was located at X, Y, Z.\u201d |\n| **2.4.2** | **Methodology Section** | Demonstrate compliance with NIST and ISO/IEC 27037. | \u2022 List all tools, versions, and settings.<br>\u2022 Describe each NIST phase and how it was executed. |\n| **2.4.3** | **Evidence Tables** | Show traceability from artefact to conclusion. | \u2022 Table: Artefact | Source | Timestamp | Location | Notes |\n| **2.4.4** | **Visualisations** | Aid comprehension. | \u2022 Timeline chart.<br>\u2022 Map with plotted coordinates.<br>\u2022 Flow diagram of data sources. |\n| **2.4.5** | **Limitations & Uncertainties** | Maintain credibility. | \u2022 Discuss possible data loss, encryption, or user manipulation. |\n| **2.4.6** | **Recommendations** | Suggest next steps (e.g., request provider logs). | \u2022 \u201cObtain 4G/5G handover logs for the suspect\u2019s number.\u201d |\n| **2.4.7** | **Appendices** | Provide raw data for review. | \u2022 Hashes, chain of custody, tool logs. |\n| **2.4.8** | **Signature & Date** | Finalise the report. | \u2022 Investigator\u2019s signature, date, and contact info. |\n\n**Justification**  \nThe *Reporting* phase must be clear, accurate, and reproducible. By following a structured format, the report can withstand cross\u2011examination and serve as a reliable record for the court.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Tool Selection Rationale\n\n| Category | Tool | Why It\u2019s Appropriate |\n|----------|------|-----------------------|\n| **Acquisition** | *Cellebrite Physical Analyzer* | Supports Samsung S23, can pull internal storage, SIM, and RAM. Provides write\u2011blocker and hash generation. |\n| | *FTK Imager* | Open\u2011source, widely accepted, can create raw images and E01. |\n| **Examination** | *Autopsy* (Sleuth Kit) | Open\u2011source, supports Android file systems, can parse SQLite. |\n| | *Oxygen Forensics Detective* | Dedicated Android extraction, automatically pulls location history, app DBs. |\n| | *Elcomsoft Phone Breakpoint* | Handles encrypted devices, can recover Google Timeline. |\n| **Analysis** | *Magnet AXIOM* | Timeline, map view, cross\u2011app correlation. |\n| | *QGIS* | GIS mapping of coordinates, heat maps. |\n| | *Wi\u2011Fi\u2011Map* / *OpenCellID* | Map SSIDs/CID to physical locations. |\n| **Reporting** | *EnCase* or *Cellebrite* built\u2011in report generator | Generates PDF/HTML reports with evidence tables. |\n| | *Microsoft Word* / *LaTeX* | For custom, court\u2011ready formatting. |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Legal & Ethical Considerations\n\n1. **Authorization** \u2013 Ensure all acquisition steps are backed by a warrant or court order.  \n2. **Privacy** \u2013 Handle personal data in line with GDPR (EU) or local privacy laws.  \n3. **Data Integrity** \u2013 Use cryptographic hashes and write\u2011blockers.  \n4. **Chain of Custody** \u2013 Document every transfer.  \n5. **Encryption** \u2013 If the device is encrypted, obtain the passcode or use a forensic tool that can bypass Android encryption (e.g., *Elcomsoft*).  \n6. **Reporting** \u2013 Avoid speculation; only present evidence\u2011based conclusions.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Potential Pitfalls & Mitigation\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| Device is *locked* or *encrypted* | Use *Elcomsoft* or *Cellebrite* to bypass Android encryption (requires passcode). |\n| Missing GPS data (e.g., GPS turned off) | Rely on Wi\u2011Fi and cell\u2011tower triangulation. |\n| Time\u2011zone mismatches | Convert all timestamps to UTC before analysis. |\n| Data deletion | Use *undelete* modules; check for *Android Trash* or *Recycle Bin* directories. |\n| Cloud\u2011only data | If the suspect used Samsung Cloud or Google Drive, request remote\u2011data extraction (subject to legal authority). |\n\n---\n\n## 7. Collection** | Obtain a forensically sound, unmodified copy of the device. | \u2022 Acquire a full **physical** image (preferred). <br>\u2022 If the bootloader is locked, fall back to **logical** extraction via a tool that can decrypt the device (e.g., Samsung Knox). <br>\u2022 Verify checksums, document chain of custody, seal evidence. | Prevents tampering, satisfies chain\u2011of\u2011custody requirements, and allows repeatability of the analysis. |\n| **2.
